Spring and Autumn

The Eighteen Nineteen Rhyme 166

— Zhanlu

The Song of Matsuoka, the Japanese representative to the League of Nations, becomes eighteen when analyzed geometrically. Now, he is being questioned by the Special Committee of the Nineteen Nations about whether Manchuria is under Chinese sovereignty. Mr. Eighteen is embarrassed! Should he say yes? Should he say no? Should he say something from the Analects of Confucius, "Yes, or is it not?" Should he say something from ancient Chinese, "Yes, yes, no, no, not so,"? Alas! The Nineteen Committee stumped Mr. Eighteen! Make an Eighteen Nineteen rhyme:

Nail head meets iron head, eighteen meets nineteen; try asking Manchuria’s rights, is it China’s? If so, then say yes, otherwise, answer no: The two words “is” and “not”, weigh more than the nine tripods. Eastern eighteen master, how to answer nineteen? The cart has hit the wall, the sleeve shows elbow again! If the word “is” is uttered, Manchuria is not his; he admits himself as the aggressor, and this determines the cause of the war. If the word “not” is uttered, the gall would be as big as a dipper; will there be the power to declare war to the League of Nations? Not unique, but a couple, two nineteen: Lord Pingyuan went to Chu, accompanied by nineteen; League of Nations Special Committee, nineteen members. The ancient nineteen people, difficult to decide is or not; adding Mr. Mao, twenty wins over nineteen. Today’s nineteen people, want to determine is or not; there is one short master, eighteen versus nineteen. Whether is or not, the ambiguity cannot last; one short eighteen, maneuvering for long nineteen. Eighteen and nineteen, who wins and who loses? The win or loss is definitive, outside the pass it is not mine!

Reading on the Tram 167

— Shiyan Ye

| Can glimpse a bit of psychology |

Driven by hunger, I have to take the tram from Jing'an Temple to North Sichuan Road at around eight o'clock every morning, and then from North Sichuan Road back to Jing'an Temple after four o'clock in the afternoon, without stopping in the cold or heat, in the wind or rain, all year round.

On the tram in the morning, most of the passengers are Chinese and foreign male and female students from primary and secondary schools. The staff in the foreign firms, banks, and companies on the Bund, a long way to go, with a book in hand, is the best way to relieve boredom. I read books every day to relieve boredom, and there are many others who use this method to pass the time.

Among the students reading books, I find that there are more foreign students than Chinese students. The books read by Chinese students are mostly in Western languages. They open the book in front of them, sometimes staring at it and reciting it silently, sometimes looking up and reciting it. It can be seen that they are focused and enjoying it. Although they also carry books on Chinese language, history, geography, etc. in their schoolbags, it is rare to see them take them out to read. From this, we can prove that today's students like foreign languages more than Chinese, and today's schools also emphasize foreign language courses more than Chinese. Around the New Year's Day a few days ago, I suddenly saw that most of them were reading Chinese books. I was surprised by their change in reading attitude. Then I thought, oh! I understand! Aren't all schools busy with big exams at this time? Winter vacation is approaching, and all subjects must be tested and ended. They use their free time on the tram to read in time. Who says they are cramming at the last minute?

People in foreign firms, banks, and companies, the books they read are of the martial arts type, of the humorous romance type. They are fully focused, not looking to the side, enjoying it without hearing the rumbling of the tram or feeling the shaking of the tram body. The ticket inspector asks them for tickets, and they don't notice. The tram arrives at the Bund, and they forget to get off. These people are fascinated by martial arts and infatuated with love. This can be seen in general!

Modern women, they don't look like students because they don't carry schoolbags. But they carry a brand new hardcover book with gold lettering and sit with it haughtily. Occasionally, they browse through it, and they really do "browse" it, flipping back and forth, as if hoping to find something in "there are houses of gold in the book, there are faces like jade in the book." Some people say: This kind of behavior is deliberately done in a crowded place to show off, isn't reading Western books very fashionable? Isn't it very prestigious in front of many people who don't know Western languages? I say: I don't think so! Why take the heart of a small person to measure the belly of a gentleman? Also, they read letters instead of reading books. They take out a piece of clean white Western paper from a Western paper envelope, with lines of horizontal text written in blue ink. Every time they read a few words, they have to look up and look at the people in the car. I say that this attitude must be because there is something secret in the letter that they are afraid of being seen, so they are so defensive. According to psychologists who have deeply studied them, this is the same psychology as those who flip through hardcover books with gold lettering.

The cooks in the mansions, carrying baskets, take the tram to the grocery market, holding Liang Shanbo and Zhu Yingtai, Meng Jiangnu, and reciting them loudly, as if reading for everyone to enjoy.

A few kinds of reading on a tram are enough to glimpse a bit of the psychology of the Chinese.

Mr. Shaw Desmond Arriving in Shanghai Tomorrow 168

The Art of Contributing 169

— Fei Ming

丨Important Notes for Contributors丨

No one wants a manuscript they poured their heart and soul into to be tossed into the wastepaper basket by the editor. The reason is simple: every contributor hopes to gain some spiritual and material reward from their submitted work.

If you want to investigate the reasons for failed submissions, you can't entirely blame your own lack of scholarship, nor can you accuse the editor of being unfair. It's simply because you've treated contributing purely as a business transaction, instead of seeing it as an "art," which shattered your hopes of publication. Therefore, we need to understand the art of contributing.

The first thing to know about contributing is to recognize your target audience, because every publication has its own personality and characteristics. Even within the Shen Bao, we know that each supplement has its own specific readership. If the manuscript you submit completely blends with the nature of the publication you're targeting, then you have a 70-80% chance of success.

Secondly, you must ensure that the submitted manuscript is original and unique, avoiding repeating what others have said and content that duplicates others' work. Especially pay attention to the writing published in the publication you intend to submit to. If your topic is something no one has written about before, then you have a great chance of gaining the applause and resonance you desire from the editor and readers.

To enrich the content of your writing, you must first focus on finding topics from your daily life. Sometimes, you will discover something you have never heard or thought of before from casual conversations with others, from reading newspapers and books, or even from your solitary musings. You can write it down at this moment, and it will be a wonderful masterpiece. Casually thinking about something and picking up a pen to write randomly cannot ensure that your submission will avoid the danger of ending up in the wastepaper basket.

Finally, pay attention to a general principle: do not let material desires overshadow your interest when writing. While you may hope to receive a considerable amount of material reward from your submission, if there is no interest, it is better not to write. Otherwise, even if your writing is published, the result will be disappointing to yourself.

Novel

The Fire of Youth 170

— Gu Mingdao

Kaijun was an honest young man. Once, his family moved to a new house. There were only his mother and him, plus a maid, a very simple household.

The afternoon of the second day after moving in, he was busy hanging mirror frames, pasting couplets, and arranging his study. His mother was helping on the side. At this moment, a young woman walked in from outside. She wore a black camel wool cheongsam with white edges around it, and a white velvet flower in her hair. Her face was delicate and appeared even more rosy and fair. Especially her charming eyes, watery and seemingly with the magic power to bewitch and captivate souls. She was not yet twenty years old, still possessing the youthful beauty of a girl. After greeting them, mother and son, she began to chat casually. They learned that she was the landlord's daughter-in-law, eloquent and friendly, making a good impression at first sight, very pitiable.

Afterwards, Kaijun's mother quietly told her son, "Beauty is fleeting, how true that is! Do you know that the landlord's daughter-in-law, named Juyun, is only nineteen this year and is already the most lonely widow in the world?" Kaijun was surprised and said, "What? Is she already a widow? Such a beautiful woman, such youthful years, how can she endure spending her life in such desolate loneliness? And what about her life in the future? Isn't her lifelong happiness already buried in the grave with her deceased husband?" After Kaijun finished speaking, he sighed deeply.

She often came over, either in the afternoon or in the evening, holding a cross-stitch frame, doing needlework while chatting with Kaijun's mother, as intimately as a family member. Gradually, she revealed her background and thoughts. According to her, she became a widow less than three years after getting married. Her husband's family was already declining, and her husband didn't know how to earn money when he was alive. Now that he was dead, her mother-in-law refused to give her a penny, only allowing her to eat plain rice, and even subjected her to constant nagging. The people in the family treated her like a stranger, and she had no one to rely on in her own family. The future was bleak and unimaginable. She was still young and wanted to do something to achieve an independent life, but she regretted that she had no education. She only graduated from elementary school and didn't continue her studies. Now, she needed it but had no opportunity to pursue education. Kaijun's mother showed her great sympathy and often comforted her with kind words. Kaijun, listening from the side, felt her life was extremely pitiful. If humans have sufficient empathy, they should think of ways to help such vulnerable people, people with such sadness buried in their hearts. (To be continued)

Where Footsteps Have Trod 171

A Tour of the Capital 172

— Peng Xuehai

Nanjing, since the success of the revolution, has donned a new outfit, like a middle-aged woman putting on modern clothes, focusing solely on appearances to flaunt herself before the shallow masses.

Several asphalt roads, wide enough to be appalling due to being based on the land of commoners, are filled with foreigners' cars driven by Chinese people. In this "Year of National Products," it's considered a unique embellishment. On the cobblestone roads beside them, rickshaws are filled with dignified armed comrades, exuding a leisurely attitude that makes you forget the stories of the volunteer army engaging in hand-to-hand combat in another corner because they lack equipment. Across the streets and along the walls and electrical poles, various slogans, both new and old, are posted and pasted. Slogans of saving the nation and resisting are the proper attitude of a land of benevolence and righteousness!

Hua Pai Lou (Ornamental Archway) is the most bustling area in the entire city, where foreign goods stores promoting national products, bookstores striving for culture, silk shops advocating thrift, and restaurants advocating reduced food intake are densely lined up on both sides, opening their mouths wide to devour people. The sidewalks are crowded with civil and military comrades wearing signs, holding their lovers in one hand and inspecting the goods in various stores with both eyes. Beggars and vagrants fill the streets and alleys. The pitiful cries for help and the agonizing cries of selling children fully represent the declining fate of the entire nation. But these sounds cannot cover up the smiles on the corners of the rulers' mouths.

Stepping into the Confucius Temple is like entering another world. Singing and dancing flourish, and life is still happy. The chaos of the shops beside the temple and the mud of the roads display the entire chaos of China. Tea houses and theaters are lined up in close rows. A few melodies of clear songs and a burst of laughter simply make one not believe in the so-called hatred of national subjugation. The famous Qinhuai River, with its whites of the eyes showing, lies coldly and unattended. Before and after the temple at the start of the new year, colorful paper lanterns fill the area, appearing lush and beautiful.

Quiet places are not non-existent, but they do not attract tourists. Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Mausoleum on Zijin Mountain, the tomb of Xiaoru on Yuhua Terrace, the Jiuming Temple for distant views, and the light boats on Xuanwu Lake are all sites with loyal martyrs. Our generation is ashamed to face the ancients!

Nanjing, a Nanjing like a riddle. Modern girls cannot compare to your charm, and beautiful young women cannot match your loveliness. Praise be to Nanjing, targeted by the enemy's cannons!

A Tour of Suzhou 173

— Zhu 𦐂

On the flat and wide Guanqian Street, the brilliance of electric lights and neon lights changes the color of the sky. Guanqian Corner at dusk already shows a prototype of Nanjing Road. Moreover, the captivating songs broadcast on the radio, such as "Selling Flowers," "Little Peach Red," and the Suzhou ballad "Sir, Miss," are played everywhere, one after another, from morning till night, spreading靡靡 melodies.

Young men of the times in suits with ironed straight lines, groups of modern girls with curly hair, roam the streets. Red velvet shirts, gray woolen coats, black velvet cloaks, red, green, black, and white clothes of various colors are reflected against the backdrop of the towering three- or four-story palace-like buildings. If it weren't for a few lurking beggars, Suzhou would truly be a splendid paradise!

In the Yuanmiao Taoist Temple, the incense smoke in the temple is densely packed all day long, gathering and not dispersing. Worshipping men and women come and go. The aromas of cooking, heating, steaming, boiling, and the various fragrant flavors of various food stalls float around to lure the silver coins and copper yuan in people's wallets, rolling away.

The strikingly dressed women selling themselves are often found under the "Notice of Strict Prohibition of Private Prostitution by the Public Security Bureau" in hotels. Indeed, according to recent investigations, the number of women selling their bodies inside and outside Suzhou has exceeded five hundred!

The cinemas and theaters in Beiju are always declared full. Whenever the iron gates are pulled open, the crowded audience always surges out like waves. The list of losses from the January 28th Shanghai Incident: "25,000 deaths, 200 million yuan in property losses" is posted on the wall of the Youth Association, but what is the use of dwelling on past events! The Suzhou people who go to the Youth Association to watch "Tears and Laughter" barely even glance at it!

US Silver Subsidiary Coin Plan 177

Ratio is One-Sixteenth

Washington, February 14th dispatch. The US House of Representatives Subsidiary Coin Committee has collected various proposals for silver subsidiary coins to create a kind of independent silver subsidiary coin with a ratio of one-tenth for deliberation. This case will form another review committee to determine the silver reserve method for this coin. Chairman of the Subsidiary Coin Committee, 生茂斯 (Sheng Maosi), said that the main point of the review committee is to stipulate the relationship between silver reserves and the treasury and to protect the treasury from maintaining the abandonment of silver. Lin Nai, the leader of domestic flour in the House of Representatives, supported Sheng Maosi's opinion, saying that he supported the coin being made of silver.

The Abolition of the "Li" and Change to the Yuan System Brings Minimal Change to Interest Rates 178

Market Situation: Yesterday's market saw little activity in both silver and copper transactions. This was largely because the rising calls for the abolition of the "li" were expected to be implemented soon. Various firms were preparing adequately, eliminating the need for further transactions. Additionally, most commercial ventures and departments had not yet expanded, resulting in a sluggish demand for funds, which was expected. Hence, the market was quiet and approaching a period of extreme calm.

Interest Rates Remain the Same: Due to the quiet trading in silver and copper, the "foreign interest" rate remained the same throughout the morning and afternoon at 7 qian, 1 fen, 4 li, 8 hao, and 7 hu and a half. This was a slight improvement of 1 hao and 2 hu and a half compared to the previous day's market price. As the abolition of the "li" drew closer, the rate could not deviate too far from the standard interest rate (7.15), preventing significant fluctuations. "Silver interest" saw limited use and few drafts, ultimately leading to ample silver supply. Interest rates remained at zero for both morning and afternoon, with no added commission.

Subsidiary Currency Stable: The Jiangnan small silver dollar fluctuated slightly, rising two li in the afternoon market to 6 qian, 2 fen, and 2 li, before dropping back two li to 6 qian and 2 fen. Trading volume was 60,000 jiao in the morning and 20,000 jiao in the afternoon. Copper coins remained at 419,000 wen, with a trading volume of 50,699 strings, equivalent to 12,100 taels of silver.

Silver Deposits Quiet: Yesterday was also quite quiet for banks in terms of silver deposits. Although the abolition of the silver system on July 1st is still some time away, most people are hesitant to open new silver accounts, making ample supply a necessary outcome.

Securities Market in Turmoil Due to Rehe Crisis; Public Bonds Fall While Troop Reduction Bonds Alone Soar 179

丨Loss of Two Yuan and Change丨

Yesterday, the public bond market at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange remained weak. The ever-changing diplomatic atmosphere caused widespread anxiety. Sellers were wary of a potential squeeze at the end of the month and were also mindful of the buying activity in the banking sector, leading to some caution. Buyers, on the other hand, feared an irreparable breakdown in Sino-Japanese relations, causing prices to fluctuate unpredictably. Trading volume was low in the morning session, with most firms adopting a wait-and-see approach. Prices fluctuated by only three to five jiao. Before the second session opened, news broke that Japan was about to issue an ultimatum, demanding the withdrawal of Chinese troops from Rehe within a specified timeframe. The Commodity Exchange, which trades futures contracts, closed early, experiencing a sharp drop of two yuan. The second session at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange saw an even more dramatic decline, with Troop Reduction Bonds plummeting by a significant three yuan. This triggered widespread panic. Later, as contracts No. 38 and No. 21 covered their short positions, the decline slowed slightly, but still remained at one to two yuan. The public bond market was turbulent. The afternoon sessions were relatively stable, but fluctuations of around one yuan persisted. The overall trend remained inconsistent. For example, Troop Reduction Bonds initially rebounded by about one yuan after opening but then lost momentum, closing with a slight gain of a few jiao. This reflected the uncertainty in the market, leading to inconsistent prices. The difference between the high and low points within each session often exceeded one yuan, indicating a growing sense of disorder in the market. By the end of the day, prices had fallen by an additional six to seven jiao to over two yuan. Contract No. 20 experienced a slight decrease of only six jiao, while Troop Reduction Bonds alone plummeted by over two yuan. The total trading volume amounted to 9,200,062 yuan, with spot trading accounting for 1,200 yuan. Troop Reduction Bonds (futures) and contract No. 19 accounted for over 2.8 million yuan. Northern and Southern Goods: High Price Increase Due to Scarcity of Honey Dates 188

丨Lanxi Bald Dates Open at 38 Taels丨

Honey dates have been in short supply recently, and inventory is thin. Therefore, the market suddenly felt a shortage. Demand exceeded supply, and prices have been rising gradually. The reason for the shortage can be traced back to the year before last. Because production was too high, prices fell to just over 10 taels by the spring of last year, causing major losses for the cargo owners. As a result, last year's production was greatly reduced, resulting in the current high prices. Yesterday, Lanxi bald dates were sold for 38 taels, and some were expecting prices to reach 40 taels. The upper and lower tiers still added rebates as usual, and the trend is strong.

Silk and Tea: Tax Exemption Approved for Silk Worm Seed Transportation and Sales in Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces 191

Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have always been famous silkworm farming areas in China. In recent years, silkworm farming in various regions has repeatedly failed, and the rural economy is on the verge of bankruptcy. Mulberry fields in Wuxi have been converted to growing rice, and farmers are very discouraged about silkworm farming. This spring, the amount of silkworm cocoons raised will inevitably be drastically reduced. The government is now actively providing relief. The silk industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces had previously requested an exemption from the Jiangsu-Zhejiang silkworm seed transportation and sales tax in order to reduce costs for farmers. It has now been learned that this proposal has been approved by the Ministry of Finance, and the heads of the Jiangsu and Zhejiang Finance Bureaus have already been instructed to order their subordinates to comply. However, this is limited to improved seeds that have passed inspection, so the improved silkworm seeds produced by various seed production areas in Jiangsu and Zhejiang can be freely transported and sold in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces without paying taxes.

Business Experience (10)

Methods for Identifying Evergreen Thick Serge - Hua An 192

(Uses) Among woolen materials, evergreen thick serge is like coarse cloth among cotton textiles. Because of its wide sales, low price, strong quality, wear resistance, and washability, it is particularly valuable because its color does not change even when exposed to sunlight or immersed in water. Therefore, all uniforms and simple suits are popular.

(Colors) Its colors vary from dark to light, including several types such as Fast Blue, Indigo, and Commercial Indigo. Fast Blue means "does not fade" or "evergreen." Indigo is a blue dye extracted from coal. Commercial Indigo is produced by processing and refining Indigo, so its dyeing price is more expensive than the previous two. However, its color is durable and does not change its original color even after being boiled with extremely strong soap, so U.S. naval officers' uniforms and summer uniform collars must be made of this type of serge. Other types are not needed. The effectiveness of Indigo is slightly less, and Fast Blue is even less. The woolen stores in the Qipan Street area of Shanghai mostly sell the latter two types (Fast Blue, Indigo). The first type (Commercial Indigo) is sold by woolen cargo companies in the Hongkou Peng Road area. The price is about one yuan more per yard than the common type.

(Quality) This type of serge is produced by various countries, especially the British products, which are superior and slightly more expensive. The products of Germany, France, Italy, the Czech Republic, Japan, and other countries are cheaper and of poorer quality. Most of the serge sold in the market is produced in Germany, France, Italy, and other countries. Such products as Tianyou, Baoke, Dongfang, Yongxing, Tianfu, and other brands are sold at prices ranging from 3 yuan to 8 yuan per yard. British-made products such as Deji, Gongping, Yongle, and Linnan range from 5, 6 yuan to over 10 yuan per yard. The price is based on the thickness of the quality, the softness and firmness of the hair, and the durability of the color. The Shanghai Zhanghua Woolen Mill also produces domestic products, which are dyed and woven in Shanghai using foreign wool. The price is about 6 or 7 yuan per yard and is usable. No matter what kind of woolen material it is, to test its quality, you can take the yarn and pull it. The stronger the pull, the longer the wool fiber, which is a good product. Otherwise, it is a poor-quality product. The products of Italy, France, and other countries are sometimes made from recycled old wool. The pulling force is weak, and it breaks as soon as it is pulled. The fiber is also short.

(Shrinkage) Thick serge shrinks a lot. Some will shrink 1 to 2 inches per yard when put in water, so it must be sprayed with water during tailoring to avoid shrinkage after washing. British-made products shrink better. Those with the English words "Shrunk" or "London Shrunk" on the loom head have already undergone the shrinking process. Indigo and Commercial Indigo also have gold lettering on the loom head or every five yards. Pay special attention when purchasing.

Free Talk

The Advantages and Disadvantages of Electricity 216

— He Jia'gan

During the Shogunate era in Japan, Christians were massacred on a large scale, and the punishments were extremely cruel, but it was not allowed to be published, and the world knew nothing about it. It was not until recent years that many historical documents were published. I once saw "The Record of the Martyrdom of Christians," which recorded the torture of Christians. They were either taken to the side of a hot spring and scalded with hot water, or a fire was lit around them and slowly roasted. This was originally a fire torture, but the person in charge moved the fire away and changed the death penalty to torture.

China has even more cruel methods. Tang dynasty novels record that a county official tortured a prisoner by roasting him with fire from all sides. If he was thirsty, he would be given vinegar to drink, which was a step further than Japan. Nowadays, when officials interrogate suspects, they use chili juice to pour into their nostrils, which seems to be a method left over from the Tang dynasty. I once saw a letter from a young man imprisoned in a reformatory, saying that he had suffered this torture before, and the pain was unbearable. The spicy juice flowed into his lungs and heart, and he had become terminally ill. Even if he was released, he would still die. This person was an army student and did not understand the structure of the internal organs. In fact, hanging upside down and pouring juice into the nose can flow into the lungs through the trachea, causing a fatal illness, but it cannot enter the heart. It is probably because this person was in pain and his senses were confused, so he suspected that it had reached his heart.

However, the cruelty of torture devices created by civilized people far exceeds these methods. There is electric torture here. Once it is applied, the whole body feels painful and about to burst, and then one faints. After a while, one wakes up and is tortured again. I have heard that some people have been tortured seven or eight times in a row. Even if they are lucky enough to escape death, their teeth will all be loose from then on, and their nerves will also become dull and unable to recover. Last year, when Edison was commemorated, many people praised the benefits of telegraphs and telephones to people, but they did not think that the same electricity can cause such great harm to some people. Lucky people use electricity to treat diseases and beautify themselves, but unfortunate people lose their lives and suffer because of it.

Other countries use gunpowder to make bullets to defend against enemies, but China uses it to make firecrackers to worship gods; other countries use compasses to navigate the sea, but China uses them to look at feng shui; other countries use opium to treat diseases, but China uses it as food. The difference in the way the same thing is used in China and the West is like this, and it is not just electricity.

Tianyun Tower 217

— Cao Juren

Tianyun Tower, the Garden of Eden on earth.

In the dim night, walking up to the highest floor of Tianyun Tower, what kind of world unfolds: a dark dome, low above, silent, deep, elusive, stars twinkling their eyes there; a new moon rising, a light haze, tall buildings covered with a layer of silk; in the distance and nearby, red, green, purple, and yellow streams of light interwoven into a colorful light network; the sound of cars and people on Nanjing Road, blown by the wind, rendered into harmonious music, echoing the light waves; this is a solemn and serene realm, the Garden of Eden in Genesis.

In the Garden of Eden, a group of naked Adams, taking off their suits, citizen clothes, intellectuals', and moralists' robes, are chasing each other there completely naked; their cheeks are red, their eyes are focused, the blood in their hearts is boiling, chasing their Eves. That group of Eves are also naked, chasing each other there completely naked; their lips are so red, their arms so smooth, their eyes so flowing, chasing their Adams.

Satan is waiting by the stairs; Eve ate the forbidden fruit, and Adam followed suit, so Satan laughed by the stairs!

Impressions of Shanghai 218

— Cheng Yirong

I have arrived in Shanghai again.

Shanghai used to be my second hometown. I left so much of my life's blood here, and I also had so many beautiful dreams here. But since I left for Hangzhou, it has been two years. In these two years, the clear face of Shanghai has jumped out of my memory and become a very blurry outline. I can no longer remember the wild dancing and singing of the rich who live solely for pleasure, nor have I forgotten the miserable sighs of the poor men wandering in the streets, the coquettishness of the girls, the sweat of the coolies, the extravagance, the licentiousness, the chaos, the crowding, I have forgotten everything.

This time, in the heavy snow, the train carried me to Shanghai again. Jumping off the train, the tragic traces of war immediately jumped into my eyes. I said to Mr. × who was traveling with me:

"Look, the war scars on the wall."

"It's been over a year."

It's been over a year, these words sharply pierced my heart, and I was lost. Hastily walking out of the station and onto the street, the street was as crowded as the station, with people coming and going, coming and going. In the center of the road, waves of brand-new cars were driving, "bo" "bo" sounding, scaring away many timid pedestrians.

Drilling through the crowd, and then coming out of the crowd, I arrived in Shanghai again, and Shanghai and I met again.

The endless crowds, the endless cars. The endless array of colorful goods displayed in the windows along the road, everything is still the same, tall foreign buildings, long shop signs, charming eyes, rogue faces, music, dancing, erotic pictures, movies, robbers, pickpockets, suicide, jumping into the Huangpu River, the stench of opium, the madness of drunkards... Everything is still the same, this is Shanghai, this is also the den of sin.

Although everything has jumped out of memory and is completely forgotten, the sentences that have been memorized will still be fluent as before when they are seen again, even if a long time has passed. So I reviewed in my heart, the current Shanghai is no different from two years ago. Ah, what a luxury, debauchery, enjoyment, ease, mixed into such a complex society.

Fine Rain Dampens Time 219

— Mei Kan

A misty drizzle is falling in the early morning, and the wheel of time has turned to spring again.

However, the cold left over from the residual winter has not yet gone away, and I cannot see the tender green grass and the newly sprouting willows. Spring, in the mundane city, is still without news. Only the black female cat kept by the apartment owner, when the weather suddenly warmed up yesterday, suddenly climbed onto the roof and called out by herself. From the sound of this "cat calling for spring", I felt that spring had indeed arrived. But today it is drizzling, and even this little bit of spring has disappeared.

The weather is changing, and this is my most unlucky time, all the joints in my body will ache, especially at night.

Spring, the rainy days of early spring, are indeed the most annoying. Time has only just reached the Lantern Festival on the lunar calendar, but people's boredom is already as deep as it is in the depths of spring. Thinking of my hometown around the Lantern Festival, it should still be quite lively, even though the old calendar has long been "revolutionized".

In my childhood, the first month was the happiest time. From New Year's Day, I wore new clothes until the month ended and the family school started. During this month, adults were busy gambling, and children were busy setting off firecrackers and watching village operas.

I remember that I was not a very good child when I was young. Once, when I was only seven years old, I gambled with some adults in the neighbor's house on the Lantern Festival, and as a result, I lost the one yuan "lucky money" that my father gave me on New Year's Eve. I was very anxious, fearing that my father would scold me if he found out, and even beat me. But I didn't dare not go home. Sure enough, in the afternoon, my mother discovered that my lucky money was gone. My mother forced me to ask, and I had to lie, saying that I was leaning on the lotus dock in the courtyard in the morning to watch the fish swimming, and unknowingly it slipped from my pocket into the water. My mother believed me very much, trusting me as all loving mothers in the world trust that their own children are good children, and quickly took fire tongs to search in the lotus dock. At that time, my heart had already been condemned!

My father, like most fathers, was more shrewd and decisive than my mother. He had already seen through my flaws and finally put on the air of a "strict father", forcing me to confess. Naturally, the result was that I confessed the truth. My father got angry and wanted to hit me. I was about to take the opportunity to escape, but my hand was already held by my father. I cried, and fortunately my mother pleaded for me, and I was finally spared a beating.

Such things now only bring a sense of loss. My kind mother is still alive, but my loving father passed away eighteen years ago. I don't know where my own childlike innocence has disappeared. The years have passed like water, and the joy of childhood can no longer be regained. Time just passes silently, passes, and when I wake up, I am already twenty-seven years old. If a person enjoys a life of sixty years, it certainly cannot be considered a premature death. According to such a number, half of his life has already passed; but what has this half of life gained?

Alas! Time just passes silently in the endless drizzle.

The Black Girl's Prayer to God 220

— By Xiao Bo'ne, translated by Yi

However, when she had taught the black girl to read and gave her a Bible on her birthday, she was probably rash. Why? Because when the black girl, who was very serious about accepting her teacher's answers, took her "knobkerrie" (Note) and strode into the African forest to find God, she took the Bible with her as a travel guide. (Note) A short club used by South African natives as a throwing weapon, with a round lump at one end.

The first thing she encountered was a "boomslang," one of the few venomous snakes that attack humans who cross their path. Originally, the teacher, because the animals were affectionate and never asked any questions, liked to keep animals. She had taught the black girl that if she could restrain herself, she should not kill anything and should not be afraid of anything. Therefore, she tightened her "knobkerrie" slightly and said to the "boomslang," "I don't know who created you! Why did he give you the will to kill me and the venom to do so?"

The "boomslang" immediately twisted its head, pointed for her to follow it, and led her to a pile of rocks, on which sat a noble-looking, burly white man, with a handsome and upright appearance, a solemn beard, and thick curly hair; both of which were as white as mica, and with a ruthless, serious expression. He had a staff in his hand, which seemed to be a scepter, a collective of large clubs and large "assegais" (Note): with this, he immediately killed the "boomslang" that was approaching him respectfully and reverently.

(Note) A type of light spear used by South African natives.

Having received the lesson of not being afraid of anything, the black girl felt her heart harden towards him, first because she thought strong men should be black, and only the ladies of the church should be white, second because he had killed her friend, the snake, and third because he was wearing ridiculous white pajamas, which reminded her of the one point where her teacher had failed to influence her, which was the obligation to wear a skirt, as she considered her own body shameful. When she spoke to him, there was a contempt in her voice.

"I am seeking God," she said. "Can you guide me?"

"You have seen him," he replied. "Kneel down now and worship me, you arrogant fellow. Otherwise, beware of my wrath. I am the Lord of Hosts; I created the heavens and the earth, and everything in between. I created the venom of the snake and the milk in your mother's breasts. In my hand is death and all diseases, thunder and lightning, storms and plagues, and all other evidence of my greatness and majesty. Kneel, girl; next time you come to me, bring your beloved child here and kill it as a sacrifice before me; for I love the scent of the first blood spilled."

"I have no children," the black girl said. "I am a virgin." (II)

Fragments from Qu Lu (IV) 221

— Zi

(6) Revolution and Confucius

I have already seen the books Confucius and Drama published. Now I will describe the book Revolution and Confucius, which is mostly recorded from official and private documents published by governments and party departments at all levels and revolutionary comrades since the "National Revolution" on the issue of Confucius (excluding personal specialized treatises on this issue). The entire book is nearly 100,000 words, with the following chapters:

A. On the sacrificial rites of Confucius and the commemoration of Confucius.

B. On the management and disposal of Confucius temples and their properties.

C. On the destruction and restoration of the Confucius Temple in Qufu.

D. On the issue of special treatment for the Confucius clan.

E. On the reading of Confucian classics in schools.

F. On various Taoist organizations.

G. On the "humiliating Confucius incident," that is, the "Zi Jian Nanzi incident."

Since the late Qing Dynasty, whether Confucianism is compatible with modern politics has become a major issue. The conservative Ye Dehui and others attacked the reformers, accusing Kang Youwei and Liang Qichao of being traitors to Confucianism, and wrote the "Yi Jiao Cong Bian." The reformer Kang Youwei also advocated the Three Protections (protecting Confucianism, protecting the race, and protecting the country) and used the birth year of Confucius for chronology. The revolutionaries (or Tongmenghui faction) represented by Mr. Zhang Taiyan advocated that Confucianism and revolution were incompatible and strongly rejected Confucianism:

"Our Chinese religion, Confucianism, was originally extremely good: that is, all religions have mysterious and difficult-to-understand words mixed in, but Confucianism is still considered clean. But it also has extremely bad points: because Confucius was originally in an era when nobles were in power, and ordinary people could not become officials. Confucius wanted to compete with the nobles, so he educated three thousand disciples to prepare them to become officials. From then on, ordinary people could indeed become officials. But Confucius was very timid. Although he wanted to compete with the nobles, he did not dare to unite with the common people to overthrow the noble political system. Although he had the words "non-hereditary officials" in the Spring and Autumn Annals, he only criticized them verbally and did not dare to implement them. Therefore, he always taught his disciples to follow others, at best to be the qualifications of imperial teachers and royal advisors, and never dared to covet the throne; and at the lowest level, even being a petty official was acceptable. When you look at Confucius's life, when he acted as prime minister, he only relied on the Duke of Lu. After traveling through seventy-two countries several times, he was at the end of his rope and returned home to retire. At that time, he even relied on the Ji family. Wasn't his ambition getting shorter and shorter every day? Therefore, the biggest stain on Confucianism is that it makes people unable to escape the thought of wealth and honor. Since Emperor Wu of the Han Dynasty exclusively honored Confucianism, the number of people who were enthusiastic about wealth and honor has been increasing day by day. If we want to carry out the revolution and promote civil rights today, if we mix in a little bit of the heart of wealth and honor, it is like a microbe that can harm the whole body, so Confucianism is absolutely unusable." | Min Zhi No. 6, Taiyan's speech record.

Mr. Zhang Taiyan was indeed a relatively progressive revolutionary thirty years ago, and he also had foresight about the corruption of the so-called revolutionary great men who used Confucianism. Alas! I was born late, and I have not yet had the opportunity to personally receive Mr. Zhang's teachings. If my book "Revolution and Confucius" is published and Mr. Zhang has the opportunity to see it, I don't know how he would feel.

Supplement to the Local Section of Shen Bao

Talking Points

They are the Fifth Class 222

— Mi Er

The severity of the current global unemployment problem is an undeniable fact. For those of us who have neither relatives who are officials nor friends in the comprador class, it is only natural that we should starve or suffer. Even if we are lucky enough to find a place to eat, we must often endure the anger of our superiors—no, the brother-in-law or other relatives of our superiors. These relatives of our superiors are what we usually call "those who wear yellow silk jackets," or what we call the "easy to see the king, but difficult to deal with the little devils."

We small clerks, in addition to doing our duty, must also pay attention to whether they have any malice towards us. Some of those who are oppressed have to swallow their anger and pretend to eat in order to get by for the rest of their lives because of their difficult circumstances. If the facts allow, some are strong-willed and unwilling to submit, and as a result, they become unemployed, become hooligans, or "eat rice from their hometown." Some have lofty ideals, endure for a while, and usually bury themselves in hard work and steadily move forward.

Once their talents are sufficient to seek other positions on their own, they immediately find ways to escape this "cage."

But aren't these "little devils" filling up every place or every organization, but filling up all of China? (Because foreigners don't like to use their own relatives to handle affairs like the Chinese.) Their power is really not small. This is really a national social problem in China. At the same time, it is also a major reason why Chinese businesses are not run well.

Since their influence in society is so great, and the harm they do to the country is so huge, we really cannot help but give them a special class. The famous British politician Burke once said that the royal family is the first class, the gentry is the second class, the common people are the third class, and journalists are the fourth class. Then, let's call this group of "little devils" the fifth class.

Before ending this article, we must also state that the relatives of superiors mentioned here of course refer to a group of people who have no ability and specialize in taking advantage of their power to grab food. As for those who make a living by their own work, of course, they are exceptions.

Moving to Xuannan, Sent to Teachers and Friends 223

— Fu Gong

Taxed house, the land in the south of the city is not yet secluded,

A humble abode is barely enough, ashamed of my planning.

Temporarily settling my pen rest next to the bookshelf,

Further nurturing potted flowers, paired with tea cups.

Good guests come occasionally to drink words,

Old vines long read through the seasons.

Pity Du Fu's days in Chengdu,

Still dreaming of the journey ten thousand miles to East Wu.

Imprisonment in the Taiwan prison, hasty like a dream,

Wife and children follow me, scattering east and west.

I am pleased that the land is remote, like Tao Qian's realm,

I am still willing to live near the market, like Yan Zi's palace.

Distraction only comes from planning for three nights,

Always wish to share a cup with affectionate friends.

Can useless materials be concerned with rise and fall?

Let us compete with poets in crafting phrases.

× Star, not only is her skill unparalleled, and her name the crown of the film world; she is also skilled in eloquence, and widely acquainted with people, and is also one of the top social butterflies in Shanghai! A noble relative of hers came from the countryside and was eager to meet her, but did not know where her mansion was. Later, with great difficulty, she found out her phone number (naturally, it could not be found in the phone book), and called her to ask, and it happened to be her who answered the phone. She seemed to disdain bending over, ignoring them completely. A poor woman with a white cloth wrapped around her head and a baby in her arms ran over to pick them up, but the modern woman glared fiercely at her and her child. The Crystallization of Blood 226

— Er Chu

He could no longer remember his mother's appearance, and at the same time, his mother could no longer remember her son's face.

When mother, under God's command, abandoned all the glory of the universe and left this defiled society, he was still in his mother's arms, living on her milk.

"Mother! My dear mother! Your son recognizes you! Your son has failed you! Your unfilial son is about to leave you! To leave you forever! Never again will I be able to wait on you as before. Mother! Perhaps your son will meet you in the afterlife! Mother... I'm leaving!" He stared at the portrait hanging on the wall and shouted excitedly.

The air in this strangely passionate garret suddenly turned cold. The birds on the few sparse trees outside the window kept chirping, as if they were also shedding tears. The sunlight gradually slanted westward, from bright to dim, and from dim to black. The portrait on the wall seemed to fade away with the sunlight.

The mournful and激烈的 military bugle, the calls of "kill, kill, kill", the sound of guns, and the sound of cannons, conveyed and reported along with the direction of the storm. Urging people from all directions to quickly take up arms and struggle for the mountains and rivers of China, never to be intoxicated under champagne! His heart was struck by it, his blood was spurting for it, in the deep dark night, in the night where he could not find a glimmer of dawn, he followed the sound of bugles, the sound of killing, the sound of guns, and the sound of cannons, daring to rush to the front line to fight.

Suddenly, he was a person with ambition and struggle, he was indeed promising, and he actually found himself in the midst of gunfire, artillery fire, and misty smoke, raising the gun he had seized from the enemy, aiming at the enemy's ranks and firing, advancing and retreating according to the orders of the military adviser, defending and attacking with the crowd of warriors. However, after all, his heart was going to break, his blood was limited, his spirit was exhausted, and he had never received military knowledge, so he was finally shot by the enemy's bullets, fell into the pile of corpses, and angrily said in pain:

"You dog party, dare to boldly fight back against us. Good... good... good! I will kill you until you beg for mercy."

So he quickly climbed up again, picked up his original weapon, and continued to fire randomly. Alas! His fate was really too bad, he was shot again, his heart finally broke, and his blood was about to run out.

"Mom... Mom...! Your... son... is... coming... to... serve... Mom... Mom...! "

Our team, our military camp, our lovely China, has lost a brave soldier.

At this time, the war horses neighed on the battlefield, the roosters crowed in the four villages, the guard dogs barked madly, and the sky gradually brightened. But he would never be resurrected again: his soul finally escaped from this terrifying battlefield and flew into his mother's arms.

Ah! This is the crystallization of his blood!

"Can't Sleep" Night 227

— Human Voice

In recent months, because of struggling in a difficult life, I have had to rack my brains as much as possible. The neurasthenia, which had not flared up for almost half a year, has taken the opportunity to entangle me this week. I really want to curse life and hate life! The most painful thing for me is insomnia every night, and almost half of the night has to be spent tossing and turning. Each time, although I try my best to calm down, discard all thoughts, and focus on listening to the ticking of the clock, concentrating on silently reciting the "one, two, three, four..." self-hypnosis method that my father taught me when I was a child, because in this way, perhaps I can make the brain nerves tired and get sleep. Trying like this, sometimes it has miraculous effects, but sometimes it is unfortunately very effective, the more I calm down, the more complex the thoughts become, the blood seems to surge up, the eyelids are wide open, the brain is more awake, the only way is to put on my clothes and climb up, lean on the writing desk, and scribble on the manuscript paper with a pen. Ah, the whip of life! Painful!

Although my dormitory is located near the countryside. Here, especially at night, there is no noisy city sound, and it is rare to have the wailing of car horns. In theory. Such a quiet place is extremely suitable for me to live in. However, in this waste year, firecrackers are continuously set off almost all night long. The most exciting thing is on this night, and it is said that this is the Lantern Festival night, the annual Lantern Festival. In the evening, because I tried my best to avoid using my brain, I took a solitary stroll in the fields for an hour after dinner. After returning home, I desperately played with the newly bought dumbbells. After nine o'clock, I fell on the bed. I was really exhausted. I thought to myself that I would definitely be able to sleep peacefully tonight. However, I was awakened by a strange, loud signal flare just as I was entering a state of drowsiness. Then, large firecrackers and long strings of firecrackers went off one after another, making noise all night long. I, in such a noisy environment, still want to sleep? With my eyes wide open, I began to think that it had been a year since I came to Shanghai. The embarrassing situation of having nowhere to rely on when I first arrived in Shanghai could not help but make me shiver deeply. The sound of firecrackers outside, far and near, was like the sound of machine guns and cannons during the war last year. Thus, the tragic situation of the war was replayed on the cerebral cortex. I thought, the people of Shanghai are really in a good mood! The huge trauma they suffered has only been a year ago, the tragic state of Zhabei is still there, but their lives seem to have reached a peaceful atmosphere, and they are having a happy New Year. Where do I even begin with this?

My heart is beating non-stop, the blood in my brain is rushing at an accelerated rate, and the firecrackers outside are still making a loud and lively noise. On this night, can I still sleep?

Classroom Sketch 228

— Wen Huan

Dang, dang...

The class bell rang, waking every young man and woman from their sweet dreams. The straight Western suits and the trembling fleshy legs under the qipaos were all swallowed into the big mouth of the classroom.

Today, the classroom is particularly lively. The front rows of seats have long been occupied by Misses, and even the last few rows of seats covered in dust are occupied by strangers. The whole classroom is packed. But they can still maintain temporary silence, except for the slight smiles on everyone's faces.

Strangely enough, it turned out to be the last lesson of this semester, and as usual, they were supposed to talk about the exam questions, so they and she came so enthusiastically, opening up the records of the entire semester. However, contrary to their wishes, the professor was late in coming. Seeing that the first class was about to end, there was not half a shadow of the professor. The raging fire was burning in the hearts of every young man and woman, and they and she could not bear the silence of stillness. For a while, the shadows of people in the hall were scattered, the noise was loud, and the chalk was dancing on the blackboard.

"Mr. ××× has asked for two hours of leave due to illness."

"::::::"

Some were pointing at the backs of the Misses in the front rows.

Some were burying their heads in reading romance novels.

Some were exchanging small pieces of paper to discuss their private affairs.

Some were fighting to watch movie advertisements and supplements.

...

...

Various different emotions, everyone is continuing to play, and happiness is waiting with pleasure.

The bell for the first class has rung, and the professor has asked for leave. In a state of disappointment and depression, that professor must be damned. After that, leather shoes closely followed high heels and fled out, and the classroom soon returned to its original emptiness.

Correspondence for Shop Employees

Conflict 230

Dear Editor:

I am a newly graduated worker in a Western clothing store, 23 years old. My father died early, and I have no brothers or sisters. When we were young, my mother sent me to elementary school and arranged a marriage for me. Now, she is nearly 60 years old and sees that I have graduated. Because there is no one at home to take care of her, she wants me to get married on a regular basis. I was afraid that the old man would be sad, so I agreed. I want to borrow some money from the boss to rush this matter. I usually feel that I lack knowledge and want to go to night school for tutoring, but I have to do night work in this store, so I cannot do it. I also want to transfer to another store so that I can have free nights to complete my reading aspirations. However, in this way, the new boss will ultimately be less familiar than the old master, and it will be difficult to borrow money for marriage. For economic reasons, the two unrelated things of "marriage" and "reading" are linked and conflict.

Sir, please help me think of a way to reconcile them so that I can fulfill my filial piety and also fulfill my reading wishes. (The following is omitted) Sincerely, Wang Xianghe

× × × ×

Editor's note: We have always opposed "borrowing money for marriage." However, because Mr. Wang's family is declining and his mother is old, we have to exceptionally support his temporarily "borrowing money for marriage" to fulfill his filial piety. However, after marriage, Mr. Wang's burden will be heavier, and the family's expenses will naturally increase several times. At the same time, he must find a way to pay off debts. Although we despise mammonism, we cannot help but advise Mr. Wang to work hard to increase his income. At the same time, we know that the income of workers in Western clothing stores increases or decreases with the amount of work. The wages in places that also do night work are naturally better than in places that only do day work. We advise Mr. Wang not to think of other jobs, but to borrow money for marriage according to your planned steps and continue to work in this store, slowly paying off the borrowed debt. "If you want peace in the world, unless everyone has food to eat." As for the level of knowledge, it is of course also very important, but you must always let this "food" take precedence. Some people's industries fall into it, and they cannot eat without knowledge, then of course food and knowledge can be mixed together. For some people, their profession has no great relationship with knowledge at all, then knowledge is only to cultivate personality. It is something for pleasure and relaxation, and even "only for entertainment." Mr. Wang's profession, I am afraid, is this kind? So we advise you not to sacrifice a portion of your working hours and be sure to join night school. If you cannot forget about knowledge at all, then read beneficial books and newspapers in your spare time, and you can also increase your knowledge.

Novel

A Family of Scholars (Continued from Two-One) 231

— Wang Zhongxian

Ruo Hua, after being poured with his love potion, didn't complain about him. She went to sound out her daughter on her feelings for You Zhong. Daiqiu said resentfully:

"I hate him! I hate even seeing his shadow! I don't want to call him uncle, because he is my enemy. I want to scold him and want to hit him a few times, but because of my mother's face, I have to forgive him!"

Seeing that her daughter hated You Zhong so much, Ruo Hua was afraid that she would really cause trouble, so it was better to send her away in marriage as soon as possible. She discussed it with You Zhong:

"Daiqiu is already eighteen years old. Sooner or later, she will be someone else's family. It is better to betroth her as soon as possible. My nephew Zheng Jiping has proposed marriage again and again. I think this young man is not bad, so let's agree to him."

You Zhong pondered for a while and said, "The daughter is yours. You can marry her to whomever you want. I cannot advise. However, you need to ask Miss clearly whether she is willing in her heart so that she will not complain in the future."

Ruo Hua went to ask Daiqiu. Daiqiu lowered her pink neck and said nothing. This is the normal state of girls, and not opening her mouth is an implicit hint of consent.

XI. I am willing to marry anyone.

Ruo Hua got her daughter's implied consent and went to agree to Jiping. Jiping had been thinking about Daiqiu for a long time. Hearing that the marriage was successful, he was so happy that he danced with joy. He immediately changed his address to call Ruo Hua mother-in-law. Seeing that Jiping was both talented and handsome, and that it was a marriage between relatives, Ruo Hua had chosen a good son-in-law and was happy in her heart. She told him to quickly find a matchmaker to carry out the engagement procedures.

Jiping went home and told his parents. The two elders knew that Daiqiu was the only daughter of Xia Zhongnan. Marrying her would allow them to inherit a share of the family fortune, so they quickly found a professional matchmaker to propose marriage. The matchmaker ran around two or three times and settled the betrothal gifts, etc. When Jiping was very happy, he suddenly received an anonymous letter. The letter read:

Mr. Jiping:

Xia Daiqiu is my lover. Suddenly, you have taken her away. How can I be willing? While you are not yet engaged, I advise you to stop the process quickly and put an end to your delusions. If you persist in your delusion, you will regret it in the future! Advanced warning, I hope you will turn back soon! Sincerely, Aiqiu

Jiping often went in and out of the Xia family and knew that Daiqiu did not leave her home. How could she have contact with men? This letter must have been written by someone deliberately joking. He didn't show it to anyone, and the marriage continued as usual. Who knew that after two or three days, another letter came, the tone of which was much more intense than the previous letter. He had no choice but to take it to his parents to discuss. His parents also said that someone was jealous and threatening, and ignored it. After three days, the date for the engagement had been set. Jiping received another letter. There was a hard bullet attached to the letter, saying that if he did not stop the marriage, he would use the final means to deal with him. Jiping's parents panicked and decided not to marry the Xia family's daughter. Since they didn't want her, they couldn't ruin Miss's reputation, so they could only politely say to the matchmaker that they intended to return the engagement because Miss's birthdates did not match. But Jiping's heart opposed the cancellation of the engagement. He still proclaimed to the outside world that he was willing to marry Daiqiu as his wife and was not afraid of any threats.

The matchmaker was very unhappy because the matter failed and she didn't get any benefits. She went to the Xia family and said a few bad words. Ruo Hua was naturally angry when she heard this, but You Zhong said coldly:

"This cannot be blamed on the Zheng family. It is to blame on Miss's birthdate being bad. Miss has a hard fate. If there are parents-in-law, she will kill her parents-in-law. If there are no parents-in-law, she will kill her husband. I knew long ago that it would not be easy to arrange a marriage. It has indeed happened now!"

Ruo Hua was also worried about her daughter, but she blamed You Zhong for not saying that her daughter had a hard fate in front of the matchmaker, because they were people who went to thousands of families. If this news spread, who would dare to marry my daughter? After the matchmaker left, Ruo Hua blamed You Zhong. You Zhong refused to admit his mistake, and the two had a quarrel. After one night, they were reconciled as before. You Zhong had an important matter to go to Beijing and would leave tomorrow.

Film Special

Horror Films of 1933 232

— Jin Moyun

Since films such as "The Old House Mystery" were welcomed by audiences, the American film industry, in order to cater to this social psychology, will strive to produce horror films from the beginning of 1933. As far as we know now, there are four types: The first is about a forbidden ape wreaking havoc in New York City. This is a work by RKO Pictures, originally titled (King Koug). The story tells of a film company capturing a giant ape on a deserted island and transporting it back to New York. The ape took advantage of people's lack of preparation, escaped the ban, kidnapped a girl, and hid in the highest 102-story building in New York. Later, it was discovered, but because there was no way to capture it, they sent a squadron of air force to bomb it to death from the air.

The second is a work by First National Pictures. It depicts the owner of a wax museum who, wanting to make the wax figures he made look like real people, steals corpses from mortuaries and cemeteries every night and smears them with a layer of wax, which is naturally very vivid and looks exactly like a living person. Later, he met a girl whose face was very similar to that of an ancient queen. He wanted to murder her and remake her into a wax figure... How the girl's life and death will turn out, let us wait for the film to be released and see the result.

The third is the story of 'The Mummy Who Crawled Out of the Tomb'. The story tells that in ancient Egypt, there was a high priest who broke the precept and fell in love with a virgin. Later, the virgin died, and he stole a book of heaven. Reciting the incantations in that book of heaven can bring the dead back to life; however, because his theft was discovered, he was buried alive, and the book of heaven was buried with him. Thousands of years later, a young explorer excavated the high priest's tomb and took out the book of heaven. Because he did not know the reason, he recited the incantations in his mouth. Suddenly, the high priest's mummy came back to life and snatched the book of heaven away. After the mummy was resurrected, he knew that the soul of his lover had been reincarnated as a human being. He also tried to kill the girl to make her soul return to her body and resurrect.

The fourth is about a crazy doctor who makes humans out of animal specimens. This is a work by Paramount Pictures. The story is taken from H.G. Wells' "The Island of Dr. Moreau." It

depicts that doctor used surgical operations making human beings. This is a terrifying masterpiece with scientific meaning.

Film Reviews

(I) A Critique of the Symphony of Life 233

— Ling He

In a story that isn't particularly unique, there's often the possibility to stage an extraordinary drama full of the meaning of life, and this film is a good example of that.

It tells the story of a doctor from a family of modest means who, through his hard work and the fervent expectations of his parents and siblings, becomes a famous physician. Of course, being a famous doctor, he inevitably carries a heavy burden for his family, and so he must diligently serve the wealthy in order to satisfy the somewhat more refined living needs of his parents and siblings. Although he possesses a benevolent nature and shows special care for the poor and sick, his old father eventually falls seriously ill. Despite his best efforts to save him, the father ultimately passes away. From then on, he can no longer trust his own abilities and decisively abandons his profession. However, he is eventually encouraged by his lover to regain his strength and fulfill his due responsibility to society.

In such a story, what we can understand is that life often presents many opportunities that make us lose confidence in ourselves, causing us to become passive. We watch people suffer while also feeling deeply uncomfortable ourselves. This kind of contradiction often exists in the course of our lives. However, we need to have faith in ourselves, because this faith can truly enhance the joy of our lives. At the same time, we can also realize here the mockery that modern society gives to life. In order to eat, we have to bow our heads to people we despise. Of course, this is a bitterness we often encounter. In fact, perhaps this is life!

As mentioned above, the theme of this play is not bad, and it is used quite profoundly by the director, so that we still have a deep stimulation after walking out of the theater. This stimulation can make us reminisce about the sorrows of life. At the same time, we can find many things that benefited from the director's skills here. Although some camera positions are inevitably ordinary, their exquisite details cannot be erased.

Secondly, what we should pay attention to is the performance skills of the protagonist Ricardo Cortez. Although the first half is just average, the second half fully reveals his brilliance. Especially the feeling of distress caused by contradictions is very vivid. The heroine Jrenne Dunne is just average, not particularly remarkable. However, Gregory Rotoff, who plays the father, is just right, so we know that every good supporting role often adds a lot of color to the play.

The lighting and sound are very good, but the dialogue is a bit too much. The setting is very suitable for the plot, but because the camera cannot be better handled, the setting appears plain.

This is a very watchable film, especially in terms of meaning, it will give us a conceptual understanding of life.

(II) A Critique of Rebound 234

— Yan Nan

Let me say at the beginning that "Rebound" is a superior film. At the very least, it offers a very frank and insightful portrayal of life and ideal love. Originally, young people often find themselves on the wrong path in love due to their environment and cannot find a way out. This film does not use ridicule to teach people; it merely uses a light touch and humor to indicate the proper course of love. Indeed, this is a bit of understanding and guidance that those immersed in the river of love need.

The plot is not amazing. It tells the story of five simple unrequited loves. A (male) loves B (female), but B loves C (male), C is partial to D (female), and D marries E (male). So C, because of unrequited love, marries B. On their honeymoon trip, they run into D in Paris from the New World. C plans to rekindle their old feelings. Unexpectedly, A provokes them from within, planning to take B for himself. B also sees C's abnormality, so she plans to divorce. Later, C repents of his mistakes and reconciles with B.

This cannot be considered a perfect comedy. I think the reunion of B and C is not a happy thing. The union of B and C in the first place was not a happy marriage at all. Since it has split again, the script insists on fulfilling them, which is inevitably far-fetched.

However, this doesn't matter, we can still deeply understand the meaninglessness of non-love unions. "Things must rot before insects breed," if a third party joins a love affair, there must first be a considerable background. One more point is that an excellent lover is not necessarily a good housewife. The reason why C abandons D for B in this film is because he recognized this point.

The director's skill lies in interweaving and contrast. Generally speaking, it is very plain. The photography can be said to be good. The light is very bright and still beautiful.

What is very special is that the clarity and loudness of the sound in this film are unmatched by any other film. Moreover, we can find many interesting things in the dialogue and small movements. Unfortunately, there is a little too much dialogue.

Among the actors, the girl (B) Ina Claire is the best. She works hard from beginning to end. Her inner facial performance is rare. The other so-called stars are just average and competent.

Anna May Wong has recently returned to the United States from England and is still working in Hollywood. This is her recent photo.

Talking About the Theme Song of Paradise In A Monastery Garden 235

— Guo Shenghong

The recently released "Theme Song of Paradise" at Guanglu is a musical and tragic British sound film. After spending two hours watching this film, it made us shed a few hot tears and have a sense of resonance before we left.

The plot is very long to tell, so I will still say the general idea: there are two British brothers who cross the ocean to Rome to specialize in music. They are both in love with the same girl, but they are engaged in open and secret struggles. Suddenly, an Italian prince jumps out of nowhere and also loves the girl, resulting in a tragic shooting. One of the brothers enters a monastery to repent, "Heaven and earth will eventually end, but this regret will last forever."

Of course, the plot is so mournful and lingering, like weeping and complaining. The director's skill is also very clever. In terms of actors, the expressions of John Stuart and Hughes Williams are commendable. Because the heroine Joan Muet is new to the screen (?), her performance is average, but she has fulfilled the responsibilities of the characters in the play.

Because this film is a musical film, the director hired a group of dancers to participate. The music is melodious and melodious, pleasant to the ear, and the background is also magnificent and gorgeous.

New Discoveries in the Chinese Scientific Community in 1933 Xia 236

—

Everyone knows that the sound movie machines used in the Chinese film industry all come from Europe and the United States; but since Yan Heming and Zhu Qingxian, and Shi Shipan successively invented domestic sound machines, although they are not enough to resist foreign products, many companies have already adopted them; however, this sound movie machine is purely derived from imported goods, and most of the raw materials used are still foreign goods.

Now I hear that Mr. Chen Zongtong has invented a purely domestic sound movie machine. Mr. Chen is from Xiangshan, Guangdong and is currently an engineer at the American Radio Corporation. He witnessed that the sound movie machines used in the Chinese film industry were all dependent on imports; in order to remedy this, he specially gathered film industry celebrities in Hong Kong to establish the Yierguang Company, set up scientific research equipment, and engaged in the research and invention of sound movie machines.

Recently, he has successfully developed a purely domestic sound machine, named "Meilefeng." The test results are very satisfactory, and it can play sound on discs or films; and the cost is low, only about 5,000 yuan per unit, which is a world apart from foreign products. Now he continues to work to increase production for film merchants to use. I hope it can come to Shanghai in the near future.

Film Novel

Flirting on Broadway Walking Down Broadway (II) 237

— Yu Qing

"Oh, don't you recognize me? I am Clark Gable." (A Hollywood superstar)

The ugly woman interjected, "Oh, Mr. Gable, I am very glad to meet you. I... I am Greta Garbo, this is my friend Gloria Swanson. Who is your friend?"

"Oh, he is Jack Cooper."

The shy man said "Nice to meet you" to the beautiful girl. The girl also replied "Hello". Just as they were striking up a conversation, the man in the cap pushed away the uglier woman, grabbed the beautiful girl's arm, and walked forward, saying, "I'll lead the way, you follow."

Walking and walking, the frivolous young man in the cap and the beautiful girl were in the front, and the shy young man and the relatively ugly woman were in the back. The relatively ugly woman often smiled at the man next to her, feeling that his appearance was indeed not bad. But the man dared not look at her directly, and often looked elsewhere. And the beautiful girl was grabbed by the annoying frivolous young man. She was very unwilling, and often turned her head to look at the shy young man.

It was probably midnight, and the two girls came back. They lived in an upstairs apartment on the corner of Ninth Avenue and 42nd Street. The two young men also followed them back. The two girls are now in the bathroom. The older girl's clothes were covered in mud, and she said with a mournful face, "I have never had a happy life. Just when I was about to be happy, I fell into the gutter."

"Hey, Millie, what's this? It will be fine in a while, go wash it off quickly. But, I never like this kind of thing, it's too immoral. Who asked them to follow us back? Especially that Mark is a bit low-class. They won't think we are Pick_Ups (playing cards), right?"

"But I really like James," Millie begged pitifully. "He also likes me. Didn't you see him jump down to save me when I fell into the gutter? Oh, Pansy, please don't say no. You're doing it for me. Didn't Mona say yesterday that you only need to take a walk on Broadway to find a man? Now we've found men, but you don't want to do it. Alas, think about it for me, it's not easy for me. We work during the day and sleep alone in the cold at night. Are we going to live like this for the rest of our lives?"

The handle on the bathroom door shook, and a woman outside shouted, "Who's in the bathroom in the middle of the night?"

"It's me, Mona, I fell in the gutter and I'm taking a shower now?"

"Haha, it's you. If someone asks me who is willing to fall in the gutter, I would say Millie. It's you, you better hurry up." After speaking, she left.

They came out of the bathroom a while later and went to Millie's room. Inside, there was an oil stove with two wicks lit, and next to it was a cabinet with many cracked cups and dishes. Mark was lying on her bed smoking a cigarette. James was sitting at the door playing with a dog. Millie ran to James, "Thank you, you saved my life. I will never forget you, whatever you want me to do, I am willing." Millie grabbed James' hand and kissed it. James shrank his hand embarrassedly.

Mark said he was hungry and asked for something to eat. Millie and Pansy looked at each other. Millie said, "I'm very sorry, there are only some raisins at home."
